<b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Giordano_Bruno&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Giordano+Bruno%22" rel="nofollow">"Giordano Bruno"</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Giordano+Bruno%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">news</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Giordano+Bruno%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Giordano+Bruno%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Giordano+Bruno%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Giordano+Bruno%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Bruno and his theory of "the coincidence of contraries" (<i>coincidentia oppositorum</i>) play an important role in <a href="/wiki/James_Joyce" title="James Joyce">James Joyce</a>\'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Finnegans_Wake" title="Finnegans Wake">Finnegans Wake</a></i>. Joyce wrote in a letter to his patroness, <a href="/wiki/Harriet_Shaw_Weaver" title="Harriet Shaw Weaver">Harriet Shaw Weaver</a>, "His philosophy is a kind of dualism &#8211; every power in nature must evolve an opposite in order to realise itself and opposition brings reunion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joyce_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joyce-81">[81]</a></sup> Amongst his numerous allusions to Bruno in his novel, including his trial and torture, Joyce plays upon Bruno\'s notion of <i>coincidentia oppositorum</i> through applying his name to word puns such as "Browne and Nolan" (the name of Dublin printers) and \'"brownesberrow in nolandsland".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Giordano Bruno features as the hero in a series of historical crime novels by S.J. Parris (a pseudonym of <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Merritt" title="Stephanie Merritt">Stephanie Merritt</a>). In order these are <i>Heresy</i>, <i>Prophecy</i>, <i>Sacrilege</i>, <i>Treachery</i> and <i>Conspiracy</i>.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bertold_Brecht" title="Bertold Brecht">Bertold Brecht</a> wrote one of his "Calendar Stories" (Kalendergeschichten) on Bruno Giordano. In <i>The heretic\'s coat</i> (<i>Der Mantel des Ketzers</i>), Brecht extols Bruno\'s unwavering honesty and selfless concern for justice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>The Last Confession</i> by <a href="/wiki/Morris_West" title="Morris West">Morris West</a> (posthumously published) is a fictional autobiography of Bruno, ostensibly written shortly before his execution.\n</p><p>In 1973 the biographical drama <i><a href="/wiki/Giordano_Bruno_(film)" title="Giordano Bruno (film)">Giordano Bruno</a></i> was released, an Italian/French movie directed by <a href="/wiki/Giuliano_Montaldo" title="Giuliano Montaldo">Giuliano Montaldo</a>, starring <a href="/wiki/Gian_Maria_Volont%C3%A8" title="Gian Maria Volont&#232;">Gian Maria Volont&#232;</a> as Bruno.\n</p><p>The computer game <i><a href="/wiki/In_Memoriam_(video_game)" title="In Memoriam (video game)">In Memoriam</a></i> features a lead character who claims to be Bruno, returned from the dead to seek vengeance.\n</p><p>Bruno features as a main character in the historical segments of <a href="/wiki/John_Crowley_(author)" title="John Crowley (author)">John Crowley</a>\'s mystical <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%86gypt" title="&#198;gypt">&#198;gypt</a></i> tetralogy of novels. The story covers his education as a Dominican and his investigation for heresy, and presents multiple versions of his execution on the Campo de\' Fiori.\n</p><p>Bruno plays a small but significant role in Martin Seay\'s 2016 novel <i>The Mirror Thief</i>.\n</p><p>Bruno is referenced in <a href="/wiki/Natasha_Mostert" title="Natasha Mostert">Natasha Mostert</a>\'s "Season of the Witch."\n</p><p>His name appears and he is recognized in several novels, including\n</p>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Children_of_God_(novel)" title="Children of God (novel)">Children of God</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Doria_Russell" title="Mary Doria Russell">Mary Doria Russell</a>.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Accidental_Time_Machine" title="The Accidental Time Machine">The Accidental Time Machine</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Haldeman" title="Joe Haldeman">Joe Haldeman</a>.</li>\n<li><i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tolosa_Gold&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tolosa Gold (page does not exist)">Tolosa Gold</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Justin_Hulford" title="Justin Hulford">Justin Hulford</a></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Picture_of_Dorian_Gray" title="The Picture of Dorian Gray">The Picture of Dorian Gray</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wilde" title="Oscar Wilde">Oscar Wilde</a></li>\n<li><i>White Fire</i> by <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Preston" title="Douglas Preston">Douglas Preston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Child" title="Lincoln Child">Lincoln Child</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>\n<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Discovery_of_Witches_(book_series)" title="A Discovery of Witches (book series)">A Discovery of Witches</a> by <a href="/wiki/Deborah_Harkness" title="Deborah Harkness">Deborah Harkness</a></i></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li></ul>\n<p>He is cited and quoted in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pauline_Hunter_Blair" title="Pauline Hunter Blair">Pauline Hunter Blair</a>\'s last adult novel, <i>Jacob\'s Ladder</i> (Church Farmhouse Books, Bottisham, 2003).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Giordano_Bruno_Foundation">Giordano Bruno Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giordano_Bruno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Giordano Bruno Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Giordano_Bruno_Foundation" title="Giordano Bruno Foundation">Giordano Bruno Foundation</a></div>\n<p>The Giordano Bruno Foundation (German: Giordano-Bruno-Stiftung) is a non-profit foundation based in Germany that pursues the "Support of Evolutionary Humanism". It was founded by entrepreneur Herbert Steffen in 2004. The Giordano Bruno Foundation is considered<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (February 2015)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> critical of religion, which it characterizes as detrimental to cultural evolution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Giordano_Bruno_Memorial_Award">Giordano Bruno Memorial Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giordano_Bruno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Giordano Bruno Memorial Award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Search_for_extraterrestrial_intelligence" title="Search for extraterrestrial intelligence">SETI League</a> makes an annual award honoring the memory of Giordano Bruno to a deserving person or persons who have made a significant contribution to the practice of <a href="/wiki/Search_for_extraterrestrial_intelligence" title="Search for extraterrestrial intelligence">SETI</a> (the search for extraterrestrial intelligence). The award was proposed by sociologist Donald Tarter in 1995 on the 395th anniversary of Bruno\'s death. The trophy presented is called a Bruno.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronomical_objects_named_after_Bruno">Astronomical objects named after Bruno</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giordano_Bruno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Astronomical objects named after Bruno">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The 22&#160;km impact crater <a href="/wiki/Giordano_Bruno_(crater)" title="Giordano Bruno (crater)">Giordano Bruno</a> on the far side of the Moon is named in his honor, as are the main belt <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">Asteroids</a> <a href="/wiki/5148_Giordano" title="5148 Giordano">5148 Giordano</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/13223_Cenaceneri" title="13223 Cenaceneri">13223 Cenaceneri</a>; the latter is named after his philosophical dialogue <i>La Cena de le Ceneri</i>  ("The Ash Wednesday Supper") (see above).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_remembrances">Other remembrances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giordano_Bruno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other remembrances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Radio broadcasting station <a href="/wiki/2GB" title="2GB">2GB</a> in Sydney, Australia is named for Bruno. The two letters "GB" in the call sign were chosen to honour Bruno, who was much admired by <a href="/wiki/Theosophy_(Blavatskian)" title="Theosophy (Blavatskian)">Theosophists</a> who were the original holders of the station\'s licence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Works">Works</span><span Tocco et H. "Bruno was burned to death at the stake for his pantheistic stance and cosmic perspective."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation" id="CITEREFArturo_Labriola">Arturo Labriola, <i>Giordano Bruno: Martyrs of free thought no. 1</i></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Giordano+Bruno%3A+Martyrs+of+free+thought+no.+1&amp;rft.au=Arturo+Labriola&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGiordano+Bruno"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Frances Yates, <i>Giordano Bruno and the Hermetic Tradition</i>, Routledge and Kegan Paul, 1964, p. 450</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Michael J. Crowe, <i>The Extraterrestrial Life Debate 1750&#8211;1900</i>, Cambridge University Press, 1986, p. 10, "[Bruno\'s] sources... seem to have been more numerous than his followers, at least until the eighteenth- and nineteenth-century revival of interest in Bruno as a supposed \'martyr for science.\' It is true that he was burned at the stake in Rome in 1600, but the church authorities guilty of this action were almost certainly more distressed at his denial of Christ\'s divinity and alleged diabolism than at his cosmological doctrines."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Adam Frank (2009). <i>The Constant Fire: Beyond the Science vs. Religion Debate</i>, University of California Press, p. 24, "Though Bruno may have been a brilliant thinker whose work stands as a bridge between ancient and modern thought, his persecution cannot be seen solely in light of the war between science and religion."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">White, Michael (2002). <i>The Pope and the Heretic: The True Story of Giordano Bruno, the Man who Dared to Defy the Roman Inquisition,</i> p. 7. Perennial, New York. "This was perhaps the most dangerous notion of all... If other worlds existed with intelligent beings living there, did they too have their visitations? The idea was quite unthinkable."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Shackelford, Joel (2009). "Myth 7 That Giordano Bruno was the first martyr of modern science".  In Numbers, Ronald L. <i>Galileo goes to jail and other myths about science and religion</i>. Cambridge, MA: Harvard University Press. p.&#160;66.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Myth+7+That+Giordano+Bruno+was+the+first+martyr+of+modern+science&amp;rft.btitle=Galileo+goes+to+jail+and+other+myths+about+science+and+religion&amp;rft.place=Cambridge%2C+MA&amp;rft.pages=66&amp;rft.pub=Harvard+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.aulast=Shackelford&amp;rft.aufirst=Joel&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGiordano+Bruno"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/> "Yet the fact remains that cosmological matters, notably the plurality of worlds, were an identifiable concern all along and appear in the summary document: Bruno was repeatedly questioned on these matters, and he apparently refused to recant them at the end.14 So, Bruno probably was burned alive for resolutely maintaining a series of heresies, among which his teaching of the plurality of worlds was prominent but by no means singular."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-gatti18-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-gatti18_11-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Gatti, Hilary (2002). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=9cYumhwTQP8C" rel="nofollow"><i>Giordano Bruno and Renaissance Science: Broken Lives and Organizational Power</i></a>. Ithaca, NY: Cornell University Press. pp.&#160;18&#8211;19. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0801487859" title="Special:BookSources/978-0801487859">978-0801487859</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">21 March</span> 2014</span>. <q>For Bruno was claiming for the philosopher a principle of free thought and inquiry which implied an entirely new concept of authority: that of the individual intellect in its serious and continuing pursuit of an autonomous inquiry&#8230; It is impossible to understand the issue involved and to evaluate justly the stand made by Bruno with his life without appreciating the question of free thought and liberty of expression. His insistence on placing this issue at the center of both his work and of his defense is why Bruno remains so much a figure of the modern world. If there is, as many have argued, an intrinsic link between science and liberty of inquiry, then Bruno was among those who guaranteed the future of the newly emerging sciences, as well as claiming in wider terms a general principle of free thought and expression.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Giordano+Bruno+and+Renaissance+Science%3A+Broken+Lives+and+Organizational+Power&amp;rft.place=Ithaca%2C+NY&amp;rft.pages=18-19&amp;rft.pub=Cornell+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.isbn=978-0801487859&amp;rft.aulast=Gatti&amp;rft.aufirst=Hilary&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D9cYumhwTQP8C&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGiordano+Bruno"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-montano1-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-montano1_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Montano, Aniello (2007).  Antonio Gargano, ed. <i>Le deposizioni davanti al tribunale dell\'Inquisizione</i>. Napoli: La Citt&#224; del Sole. p.&#160;71. <q>In Rome, Bruno was imprisoned for seven years and subjected to a difficult trial that analyzed, minutely, all his philosophical ideas. Bruno, who in Venice had been willing to recant some theses, become increasingly resolute and declared on 21 December 1599 that he \'did not wish to repent of having too little to repent, and in fact did not know what to repent.\' Declared an unrepentant heretic and excommunicated, he was burned alive in the Campo dei Fiori in Rome on Ash Wednesday, 17 February 1600. On the stake, along with Bruno, burned the hopes of many, including philosophers and scientists of good faith like Galileo, who thought they could reconcile religious faith and scientific research, while belonging to an ecclesiastical organization declaring itself to be the custodian of absolute truth and maintaining a cultural militancy requiring continual commitment and suspicion.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Le+deposizioni+davanti+al+tribunale+dell%27Inquisizione&amp;rft.place=Napoli&amp;rft.pages=71&amp;rft.pub=La+Citt%C3%A0+del+Sole&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.aulast=Montano&amp;rft.aufirst=Aniello&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGiordano+Bruno"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-birx-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-birx_13-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Birx, James (11 November 1997). <a class="external text" href="http://www.theharbinger.org/xvi/971111/birx.html" rel="nofollow">"Giordano Bruno"</a>. <i>Mobile Alabama Harbinger</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">28 April</span> 2014</span>. <q>To me, Bruno is the supreme martyr for both free thought and critical inquiry&#8230; Bruno\'s critical writings, which pointed out the hypocrisy and bigotry within the Church, along with his tempestuous personality and undisciplined behavior, easily made him a victim of the religious and philosophical intolerance of the 16th century. Bruno was excommunicated by the Catholic, Lutheran and Calvinist Churches for his heretical beliefs. The Catholic hierarchy found him guilty of infidelity and many errors, as well as serious crimes of heresy&#8230; Bruno was burned to death at the stake for his pantheistic stance and cosmic perspective.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Mobile+Alabama+Harbinger&amp;rft.atitle=Giordano+Bruno&amp;rft.date=1997-11-11&amp;rft.aulast=Birx&amp;rft.aufirst=James&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.theharbinger.org%2Fxvi%2F971111%2Fbirx.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGiordano+Bruno"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-britannica.com-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-britannica.com_14-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-britannica.com_14-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.britannica.com/biography/Giordano-Bruno" rel="nofollow">"Giordano Bruno"</a>. <i>Encyclop&#230;dia Britannica</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica&amp;rft.atitle=Giordano+Bruno&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.britannica.com%2Fbiography%2FGiordano-Bruno&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGiordano+Bruno"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The primary work on the relationship between Bruno and Hermeticism is Frances Yates, <i>Giordano Bruno and The Hermetic Tradition</i>, 1964; for an alternative assessment, placing more emphasis on the Kabbalah, and less on Hermeticism, see Karen Silvia De Leon-Jones, <i>Giordano Bruno and the Kabbalah</i>, Yale, 1997; for a return to emphasis on Bruno\'s role in the development of Science, and criticism of Yates\' emphasis on magical and Hermetic themes, see Hillary Gatti (1999), <i>Giordano Bruno and Renaissance Science</i>, Cornell.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Alessandro G. He also suggests it is likely that Bruno kept the tonsure even after this point, showing a continued and deep religious attachment contrary to the way in which Bruno has been portrayed as a martyr for modern science. Instead, Gosselin argues, Bruno should be understood in the context of reformist Catholic dissenters. Edward A. Gosselin, "A Dominican Head in Layman\'s Garb? A Correction to the Scientific Iconography of Giordano Bruno", in <i>The Sixteenth Century Journal</i>, Vol. 27, No. 3 (Autumn, 1996), pp. 673&#8211;678.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Dorothea Waley Singer, <i>Giordano Bruno, His Life and Thought</i>, New York, 1950 "Following the northern route back through Brescia, Bruno came to Bergamo where he resumed the monastic habit. He perhaps visited Milan, and then leaving Italy he crossed the Alps by the Mont Cenis pass, and came to Chamb&#233;ry. He describes his hospitable reception there by the Dominican Convent, but again he received no encouragement to remain, and he journeyed on to Lyons. Bruno\'s next movements are obscure. In 1579 he reached Geneva."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-ReferenceA-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ReferenceA_22-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ReferenceA_22-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Virgilio Salvestrini, <i>Bibliografia di Giordano Bruno</i>, Firenze, 1958</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Dorothea Waley Singer, <i>Giordano Bruno, His Life and Thought</i>, New York, 1950; Singer points out in a footnote that Bruno\'s name appears in a list, compiled one hundred years later, of Italian refugees who had belonged to the Protestant church of Geneva. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">8 May</span> 2014</span>. <q>At the time such a move did not seem to be too much of a risk: Venice was by far the most liberal of the Italian states; the European tension had been temporarily eased after the death of the intransigent pope Sixtus V in 1590; the Protestant Henry of Bourbon was now on the throne of France, and a religious pacification seemed to be imminent.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica&amp;rft.atitle=Giordano+Bruno&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.britannica.com%2FEBchecked%2Ftopic%2F82258%2FGiordano-Bruno%2F883%2FFinal-years&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGiordano+Bruno"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"II Sommario del Processo di Giordano Bruno, con appendice di Documenti sull\'eresia e l\'inquisizione a Modena nel secolo XVI", edited by Angelo Mercati, in <i>Studi e Testi</i>, vol. 101.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Luigi Firpo, Il processo di Giordano Bruno, 1993.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This is discussed in Dorothea Waley Singer, <i>Giordano Bruno, His Life and Thought</i>, New York, 1950, ch. 7, "A gloating account of the whole ritual is given in a letter written on the very day by a youth named Gaspar Schopp of Breslau, a recent convert to Catholicism to whom Pope Clement VIII had shown great favour, creating him Knight of St. Peter and Count of the Sacred Palace. Schopp was addressing Conrad Rittershausen. He recounts that because of his heresy Bruno had been publicly burned that day in the Square of Flowers in front of the Theatre of Pompey. He makes merry over the belief of the Italians that every heretic is a Lutheran. It is evident that he had been present at the interrogations, for he relates in detail the life of Bruno and the works and doctrines for which he had been arraigned, and he gives a vivid account of Bruno\'s final appearance before his judges on 8th February. To Schopp we owe the knowledge of Bruno\'s bearing under judgement. When the verdict had been declared, records Schopp, Bruno with a threatening gesture addressed his judges: "Perchance you who pronounce my sentence are in greater fear than I who receive it." Thus he was dismissed to the prison, gloats the convert, "and was given eight days to recant, but in vain. So today he was led to the funeral pyre. When the image of our Saviour was shown to him before his death he angrily rejected it with averted face. Thus my dear Rittershausen is it our custom to proceed against such men or rather indeed such monsters."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Fitzgerald2007-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Fitzgerald2007_34-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Fitzgerald, Timothy (2007). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=b67p1VdF_OoC&amp;pg=PA239" rel="nofollow"><i>Discourse on Civility and Barbarity</i></a>. Routledge. p.&#160;419. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1317677666" title="Special:BookSources/978-1317677666">978-1317677666</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">29 March</span> 2015</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+Cosmology+%28Routledge+Revivals%29%3A+Historical%2C+Philosophical%2C+and+Scientific+Foundations+of+Modern+Cosmology&amp;rft.pages=419&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft.isbn=978-1317677666&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DEP9QAwAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA419&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGiordano+Bruno"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/> Bruno (from the mouth of his character Philotheo) in his <i>De l\'infinito universo et mondi</i> (1584) claims that "innumerable celestial bodies, stars, globes, suns and earths may be sensibly perceived therein by us and an infinite number of them may be inferred by our own reason."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Max_Tegmark" title="Max Tegmark">Max Tegmark</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://wayback.archive-it.org/all/20081217134224/http://www.hep.upenn.edu/~max/multiverse.pdf" rel="nofollow">Parallel Universes</a>, 2003</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Max Bernhard Weinsten, <i>Welt- und Lebensanschauungen, Hervorgegangen aus Religion, Philosophie und Naturerkenntnis</i> ("World and Life Views, Emerging From Religion, Philosophy and Nature") (1910), p. 321: "Also darf man vielleicht glauben, da&#223; das ganze System eine Erhebung des Physischen aus seiner Natur in das G&#246;ttliche ist oder eine Durchstrahlung des Physischen durch das G&#246;ttliche; beides eine Art Pandeismus. Und so zeigt sich auch der Begriff Gottes von dem des Universums nicht getrennt; Gott ist naturierende Natur, Weltseele, Weltkraft. Da Bruno durchaus ablehnt, gegen die Religion zu lehren, so hat man solche Angaben wohl umgekehrt zu verstehen: Weltkraft, Weltseele, naturierende Natur, Universum sind in Gott. Gott ist Kraft der Weltkraft, Seele der Weltseele, Natur der Natur, Eins des Universums. Bruno spricht ja auch von mehreren Teilen der universellen Vernunft, des Urverm&#246;gens und der Urwirklichkeit. Und damit h&#228;ngt zusammen, da&#223; f&#252;r ihn die Welt unendlich ist und ohne Anfang und Ende; sie ist in demselben Sinne allumfassend wie Gott. Aber nicht ganz wie Gott. Gott sei in allem und im einzelnen allumfassend, die Welt jedoch wohl in allem, aber nicht im einzelnen, da sie ja Teile in sich zul&#228;&#223;t."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Seife, Charles (1 March 2000). <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130608054739/http://news.sciencemag.org/sciencenow/2000/03/01-04.html" rel="nofollow">"Vatican Regrets Burning Cosmologist"</a>. <i>Science Now</i>.
